<center><b><h3>List of Known Trans-Neptunian Objects</h3></b>
(and other outer solar system objects)<br>
last updated 13 July 2019
</center><p></p><p>
Notes:
</p><ul>
<li> Table includes TNOs, SDOs, and Centaurs listed by the MPC as of 24 May 2019, plus other unusual asteroids with aphelion distances greater than 7.5 AU, plus several additional reported objects without MPC designations.
</li><li> Dynamical classifications are <i>not authoritative</i>, reflecting ambiguity in the literature regarding delineations between classes.  The classifications given here are based on:  <i>Distant Minor Planets</i> MPECs and MPC listings; Elliot et al., 2005, <i>Astronomical Journal</i>, 129:1117-1162; Buie et al. on line listing (DES object classifications); Gladman et al., 2008, in <i>The Solar System Beyond Neptune</i>, 43-57; Jewitt, 2005, <i>Astronomical Journal</i>, 129:530-538; Sheppard (definitions of extreme SDOs); and JPL Small Bodies Node.  In some cases classifications are ambiguous.
</li><li> Orbital elements are from MPC listings, supplemented by discovery publications for objects lacking MPC designations.
</li><li> Diameter values marked by  ?are estimated assuming an albedo of 0.09 (or for secondary components, assuming the same albedo as the primary).  Remaining diameter values have been determined by various methods (combined optical/thermal observations, dynamical fits/assumed densities for binaries, direct imagery, or stellar occultation).  For sources see <a href="http://www.johnstonsarchive.net/astro/tnodiam.html">this page</a>.
</li><li> B-R magnitude is the difference between blue filter magnitude and red filter magnitude; values greater than 1.03 indicate spectra redder than that of the Sun.
</li><li> Taxonomic type is from Belskaya et al., 2015, <i>Icarus</i>, 250:482-491.
</li><li> For sources regarding companions see <a href="http://www.johnstonsarchive.net/astro/asteroidmoons.html">pages here</a>.  Objects with postulated but undetected companions are indicated with "?" under "known add'l components".
</li><li> See end of table for other sources.
</li></ul>
<p></p><p>
Object counts by available data are as follows:
